CURRENT CODE:
```ts
const parentElement = computed(() => gridContainer.value?.parentElement)
const { width: parentWidth, height: parentHeight } = useElementSize(parentElement)

const gridScale = computed(() => {
  const naturalWidth = 1330  // 5 columns + gaps
  const naturalHeight = 416   // 2 rows + gap
  
  const widthScale = parentWidth.value / naturalWidth
  const heightScale = parentHeight.value / naturalHeight
  
  // Use smaller to fit both dimensions
  return Math.max(0.5, Math.min(1.2, Math.min(widthScale, heightScale)))
})
```

PROBLEM: On small screens, grid is way too small even though there's plenty of height available.

QUESTION: What is the root cause preventing proper scaling? Consider:
1. Which element should we measure?
2. Is measuring the max-w-5xl wrapper the issue?
3. Should we measure the theater container (absolute inset-0 p-8) instead?
4. Are the natural dimensions wrong?
5. Does transform:scale() affect layout space vs visual space?

Identify the SINGLE root cause and the fix."
